---
title: An Experimental Guide to Image Inpainting
slug: inpainting
summary: This showcases different approaches to Image Inpainting randing from Context Encoders over Unet to Partial Convolution.
status: draft
--- 


## Naive Approach
The Input of the network is an image with areas erased. Loss is the MSE between the network's output and the original image.
## U-net [@@ronneberger2015unet]
U-net is a generative vision model which meaning it takes an image as input and outputs an image. 
While U-net was developed for medical image segmentation (which basically means generating the segmentation image), we can also use it for tasks like super-resolution, Style transfer, and in my case Inpainting. 

The idea is to downsample to a latent space with an encoder and then upsample from the latent space with the decoder. 
As the latent space does not provide enough information to optimally upsample, skip connections between encoder and decoder are introduced. This means every time the grid size is halved, the activations will be copied over and concatenated in the upsampling part of the U-net. 


But letâ€™s look at some best-practices examples. First, while the "official" U-net from the paper is a promising network, the encoder is not state of the art, as ResNet was not invented yet. If we want to leverage the residual connections of ResNet to have both long-term skip connection between encoder and decoder and short-term skip connections in the individual ResNet Blocks. We, therefore, want to switch out the encoder with a ResNet architecture. When using fastai we can simply use `unet_learner(dls_gen, models.resnet34)` to create a U-net with a resnet34 backbone, meaning we are downsampling from our 3 channel image with a resnet34 architecture. 


Some Parameters can be set to improve the performance:

* `blur=True` might reduce checkerboard artifacts by "zero-hold padding" the inputs. This means adding a `nn.ReplicationPad2d((1,0,1,0))` and `nn.AvgPool2d(2, stride=1)` to each conv layer.
* `self_attention=True` ([@zhang2019self]) [More details](/attention)


For upsampling, there are also multiple variants that are worth trying [@dumoulin2016guide]

* Transposed or Stride Half Convolutions (also deconvolutions): Add a zero-padding between all pixels. The problem is that a lot of computation is wasted by this.</br>

* **Nearest Neigboor Interpolation**: Instead of zero values as in transposed convolutions, we generate the values of the extra pixels with Nearest Neighbor interpolation. This usually works better than transposed convolutions, but also introduces artifacts.
* **Pixel Shuffle**: For increasing inputs by a factor $r$ we want to have feature maps with $r^2$ channels. We calculate the convolution for each pixel and channel and shuffle them as shown in the graphic. This is also known as sub-pixel convolutions and has the advantage of the convolution is performed on the original smaller image instead of a larger interpolated image. This means that the performance is better and training faster.[@shi2016real]</br>

* To really get rid of the checkerboard patterns, we have to do an initialization with *Initialized to Convolution NN Resize*[@aitken2017checkerboard]. Each of the $r^2$ channels will initially get the same random initiation.


### Code
<details><summary>
Creating a U-Net-Learner in fastai
</summary>

```python
    def create_gen_learner():
    return unet_learner(dls_gen,
                        models.resnet34,
                        self_attention=True,
                        blur=True,
                        act_cls = Mish,
                        y_range=(-3.,3.),
                        opt_func=ranger,
                        loss_func=MSELossFlat())

```

</details>

### Results
While training we see that the generator is unable to improve his performance as the discriminator is stuck. A visual examination of the generated images shows clear patches with the generator unable to reproduce the underlying structure. This is likely due to the loss function being only pixel-wise. 

![Results of Unet](/images/inpainting/unetresults.png)

A common approach to having a loss of the style and features is the **Perceptual Loss.** ([@johnson2016perceptual]) Using a pre-trained model (in this case VGG16 or VGG19) this adds a feature loss by comparing activation for the content target $y_c$ (also called Ground Domain Image) and transform network output $\hat{y}$ and a style loss by comparing the activations between style target $y_s$ and $\hat{y}$ via the Gram Matrix.

### Spectral Norm
The second contribution is based on [@miyato2018spectral], [@zhang2019self] propose norming not only the Discriminator but also the Generator, as in their tests this increases overall performance.
## Context Encoders GAN [@pathak2016context]

## Partial Convolution [@liu2018image]
The naive U-Net Approaches failed due to a lack of texture but in literature, we can see that similar approaches are unable to provide good results. You can often see obvious color contrasts or artificial edges surrounding the hole.  

[@liu2018image] propose the use of **Partial Convolutional** Layers, comprising of a masked and re-normalized convolution operation followed by a mask-update step. The convolutional results of the masked region depend only on the non-masked region and the mask is iteratively reduced with each reconstruction step. This means that this kind is completely agnostic to the values of the hole. (Other techniques require the holes to be zero, 0, 127.5 (median pixel value), or the mean ImageNet Pixel Value).
Padding can also be replaced by Partial Convolution so that outside values will not be affected by invalid values

*Overview of Network Structure*

After Augmentation both the mask $\mathbf{M}$ and the masked image ( $\mathbf{M}*\mathbf{I}_{gt}$ ).The structure of the network is U-net-like with skip connections in the decoder concatenating both the two feature maps and the two masks.


A total of 6 loss functions are combined to calculate the total Loss: 

$$\mathcal{L}_{\text {total }}=\mathcal{L}_{\text {valid }}+6 \mathcal{L}_{\text {hole }}+0.05 \mathcal{L}_{\text {perceptual }}+120\left(\mathcal{L}_{\text {style }_{\text {out }}}+\mathcal{L}_{\text {style }_{\text {comp }}}\right)+0.1 \mathcal{L}_{\text {tv }}$$

The Loss functions are marked in the overview image above. For Syntax the following symbols are used:

* $\mathbf{I}_{g t}$ the Ground Truth with $N_{\text{I}_{gt}}$ elements (Channels x Width x Height),
* $\mathbf{I}_{out}$ the network prediction,
* $\mathbf{M}$ the mask with 0 for holes,
* $\mathbf{I}_{comp}$ the ground truth image but the pixels of the mask replaced by the network prediction and
*  $\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{*}}$ the activation map of the p-th layer of an Image-Net-pre-trained VGG-16.

With this, the Losses are 

1. *Pixel Loss Hole:* $$\mathcal{L}_{\text {hole }}=\frac{1}{N_{\text {I }_{g t}}}\left\|(1-M) \odot\left(\mathbf{I}_{\text {out }}-\mathbf{I}_{g t}\right)\right\|_{1}$$ 
2. *Pixel Loss non-masked:* $$\mathcal{L}_{\text {valid }}=\frac{1}{N_{\text {I }_{g t}}}\left\|M \odot\left(\mathbf{I}_{\text {out }}-\mathbf{I}_{g t}\right)\right\|_{1}$$ 
3. *Perceptioal Loss (Feature):* $$\mathcal{L}_{\text {perceptual }}=\sum_{p=0}^{P-1} \frac{\left\|\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{o u t}}-\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{g t}}\right\|_{1}}{N_{\Psi_{p}^{\mathrm{I}} g t}}+\sum_{p=0}^{P-1} \frac{\left\|\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{c o m p}}-\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{g t}}\right\|_{1}}{N_{\Psi_{p}^{\mathrm{I}} g t}}$$ 
4. *Perceptioal Loss (Style):* $$\mathcal{L}_{\text {style }_{\text {out }}}=\sum_{p=0}^{P-1} \frac{1}{C_{p} C_{p}}\left\|K_{p}\left(\left(\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{o u t}}\right)^{\top}\left(\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{o u t}}\right)-\left(\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{g t}}\right)^{\top}\left(\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{g t}}\right)\right)\right\|_{1}$$ and 
5. *Perceptioal Loss (Style) II:* $$\mathcal{L}_{\text {style }_{\text {comp }}}=\sum_{p=0}^{P-1} \frac{1}{C_{p} C_{p}}\left\|K_{p}\left(\left(\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{c o m p}}\right)^{\top}\left(\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{c o m p}}\right)-\left(\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{g t}}\right)^{\top}\left(\Psi_{p}^{\mathbf{I}_{g t}}\right)\right)\right\|_{1}$$ by using autocorrelation on each feature map, assuming that the feature map $\Psi_{p}$ is of size $\left(H_{p} W_{p}\right) \times C_{p}$ and normed by the factor $K_p=\frac{1}{C_p H_p W_{p}}$.
6. *Total Variation Loss:* $$\mathcal{L}_{t v}=\sum_{(i, j) \in R,(i, j+1) \in R} \frac{\left\|\mathbf{I}_{c o m p}^{i, j+1}-\mathbf{I}_{c o m p}^{i, j}\right\|_{1}}{N_{\mathbf{I}_{c o m p}}}+\sum_{(i, j) \in R,(i+1, j) \in R} \frac{\left\|\mathbf{I}_{c o m p}^{i+1, j}-\mathbf{I}_{c o m p}^{i, j}\right\|_{1}}{N_{\mathbf{I}_{c o m p}}}$$ of the mask border.


## How can we check our results?
* Per Pixel MSE Loss
* Inception Distance (KL divergence  between the conditional class distribution and the marginal class distribution. Higher= Better)
* Frechet Inception (Intra-FID): Wasserstein-2 distance between the generated images and the real images (but also between all generated and real images of one class = Intra FID), lower= better

## Questions

* What is a good conditioned GAN? (Miyato et al., 2018).)
* separate learning rates (TTUR) for Disc and Gen [@heusel2017gans]
* State of the art is [@miyato2018spectral]
* What is a projection conditioned discriminator? [@miyato2018cgans]
* What is the conditional batch norm. 
* Can Contrastive Patchwise Loss be used as an additional Loss Function (CUT)
